Free Talk

Making Literature with Strawberries 199

— Gu Fei

Some say that a writer from a certain social stratum can only write about that social stratum, because they cannot be untrue to their lives.

At first glance, this high-sounding theory is quite admirable. No matter how "tyrannical" a critic is, they wouldn't "order" a writer to tell lies.

But upon closer examination, it seems somewhat doubtful. First, according to this theory, it seems as if a person's social existence is predetermined by the King of Hell in a previous life and cannot be changed. But the actual situation is not necessarily so. For example, wealthy farmers become coolies, students enter factories, and there are extreme examples of high-ranking scholars pulling rickshaws. Of course, writers are the excellent members of the nation and should be able to do as they please, but if he or she is also a social being, how can they always sit in a fragrant and melodious place like "Mount Tai Stone Dare to Act"? Second, a writer from a certain social stratum may not necessarily understand the life of that social stratum. There are many examples of this, such as the writers who are now shouting about petty-bourgeois revolutionary literature, none of whom can fully portray the suffering of the petty bourgeoisie. Similarly, although not from that social stratum, one can break into, integrate into, and grow in that social stratum. Like Fadeyev, Barbusse, Kobayashi Takiji...

What is the key here? The answer is the same: it depends on whether the writer is true to life. But there is also a slight difference: the "life" referred to here does not only refer to the narrow experience of a permanently unchanged abstract thing, but to the practice associated with the dynamic society. And this includes the dynamic role of human cognition.

Today I read Ritsuno Nobuyuki's "Strawberries" in the July issue of "Chuo Koron." On such a hot day, seeing the word "strawberries" easily brings to mind "strawberry milk," a good thirst quencher. But there is none of that fragrance in this novel. Instead, using strawberry cultivation as the main focus of the story, it depicts the changes in the rural economy, the hardships of farmers, the tragedies caused by hardship and desperate labor, and the process of awakening. The analysis of the rural social structure, the explanation of various planting problems such as fertilizer and climate, and the depiction of farmers' emotions are not something that can be achieved solely with a little experience. Needless to say, Ritsuno is an intellectual, but his creative activities have not been confined by a small range of experience. This novel illustrates his efforts.

However, our "writers," apart from sitting in their rooms and writing big articles on white paper about what banner to raise, do not bother with things like strawberry research.

Akita Ujaku's Fifty Years 200

— Suo Yuan

Akita Ujaku, known as the "Japanese Gorky," is commemorating the fiftieth anniversary of his birth this year.

Akita was born in 1883 in Aomori Prefecture in northeastern Japan. During the Russo-Japanese War, influenced by the anti-war arguments of the time, he became a supporter of the early socialist movement in Japan, including figures such as Katayama Sen and Kotoku Shusui. He did not appear on the literary scene until after 1905, initially writing poetry and novels, gradually developing an interest in theatrical creation, and successively publishing collections such as "Phantoms and Nocturnes," "Buried Spring," and "Young Playwrights."

During World War I, the successive deaths of his father and son, and the gradual impoverishment of his life, plunged him into a state of pessimism and nihilism for a time. At that time, he studied Tolstoy's religious theories and Indian philosophy. During this period, he published "Three Souls" and "The Death of Buddha."

From 1919 to 1926, Japan was truly a difficult autumn. The impoverishment of the entire nation after the Great War triggered the democracy movement, and there was also a "people's art" movement in culture. This movement soon developed into the so-called "art of the Fourth Estate." Regarding this period, Akita wrote in his autobiography "My Fifty Years": "I heard the sound of boiling from beneath the ground I was walking on."

In 1921, the Light Movement emerged, followed by the establishment of the "Sower" group. It was also during this period that he studied Esperanto with extraordinary enthusiasm. In his own words: "Esperanto transformed me into a completely different person. I felt that I was saved by Esperanto. I finally became a cheerful and lively world citizen. The literary world is simply a narrow and disgusting place."

In October 1927, Akita was invited to the Soviet Union as a state guest to attend the tenth anniversary of the revolution.

During his stay in Russia, he used Esperanto to visit various places and wrote "Young Soviet Union" after returning home, which was praised as "Even young people who are proficient in Russian may not be able to observe so precisely."

From the "people's art" movement to the present, he has been moving forward with the times without taking a step back. He personally experienced the various stages in various fields of the modern Japanese cultural movement. He personally "sowed seeds" and nurtured the emerging Japanese culture. He served as the director of the International Culture Research Institute, the director of the Proletarian Science Research Institute, the director of the New Education Research Institute, the chairman of the Central Committee of the World Esperanto Association, the chairman of the Anti-Religious League when it was founded, and was also an outstanding literary and theatrical writer and a leader of the Japan-Russia Cultural Exchange Association. We cannot fail to mention his name when discussing the modern cultural movement in Japan.

But he is not a writer who, like Gorky, came from the working class. In his fifty-year career, he experienced painful "self-struggles" and a series of hard-fought struggles as a revolutionary intellectual. Perhaps because of this, we feel even more lovable and have a sense of intimacy.

What we find most interesting is that, at such an old age, he enthusiastically studied Esperanto and said, "I was saved by Esperanto." We, who do not have a personal experience of the gloomy intellectual world of Japanese capitalist society at the end of the Meiji era and the beginning of the Taisho era, probably cannot fully understand it. But if we think of how Arishima Takeo and Akutagawa Ryunosuke solved their problems with "death," and how Mushanokoji Saneatsu degenerated in order to find a way out, in contrast, "I was saved by Esperanto" is not only not excessive, but is it not the most truthful confession?

Recently, at a gathering in the Tokyo cultural world to celebrate his fiftieth birthday, he agreed to write a masterpiece using the process of the Japanese intellectual class's struggle over the past two or three decades as the theme. When the news came, we couldn't help but sincerely congratulate him on his fiftieth birthday and wish him good health!

Essentials of Climbing the Literary Ladder 201

— Lin Yizhi

Recently, a bookstore published a book called "Essentials of Climbing the Literary Ladder." Because I wanted to use that dollar for something else, I have not yet had the good fortune to read it. Fortunately, I have seen quite a few writers climbing the ladder. From their actions, I can learn a few techniques for climbing the ladder. I jotted down a few at random and used the topic to write an article on "Essentials of Climbing the Literary Ladder." Perhaps some people who are eager to climb the ladder but don't have the money to buy the book might as well take a look.

An unknown writer who wants to become famous has to interact with famous people. If the famous person pays attention to you, you can write "my friend" and the like in your articles. If they ignore you, you can scold them. Fortunately, you don't need much reason to scold people. For example, place of origin, age, or even family relationships can all be used as material for scolding. Anyway, people will pay attention when they see you dare to scold someone.

When writing works, you have to see what others like. If people like to read sexual history, you specialize in writing love novels with triangles and quadrangles and swollen lower bodies. You must write about women as being very horny and able to provoke men. This way, your books will sell well, and readers will not show any signs of fatigue.

You can also open your own bookstore and run your own magazine. You can publish whatever nonsense or nauseating things you write as if they were interesting. You can also ask someone to translate your work into a foreign language and then brag that your work is international.

Sometimes, if the opportunity arises, you can also make a change and write some riot novels, but you must always be careful. If there is even a slight rumor, you must quickly write a confession and a letter of repentance, stating that you are no longer involved. At that time, you raise a self-made banner of some sort to show that your position is firm.

On a smaller scale, you can specialize in being an intelligence gatherer, saying that so-and-so is so-and-so's pseudonym, and that so-and-so lives there. This way, you will also become famous. Not only do you gather information about others, but you can also publish your own information and put it together with famous people, and even publish more photos.

All of the above are just examples. However, the most important thing is to specialize in one of them, and then you will have the technique to climb the ladder. In ancient times, scholars studied hard for ten years in order to achieve fame and fortune. Today, people sharpen their heads just to make a living. In the past, writers sold large characters; today, writers sell small characters. It's all the same: selling. Who cares about face? Only those fools will truly do literature. Their contribution is to insist on life and explore reality to the end. In the end, they will end up with no trace of their death. You must never imitate them!

Teatime Chat 202

— Wu Qiushan

Drinking tea is the most democratic thing. Those who have leisure, of course, use tea as a gift and as a good way to pass the time. Even ordinary people, such as farmers and woodcutters in villages, and workers in the city, are no different. In the faint cold dusk, or in the sweltering evening, a few friends go to the tea house together, brew a pot of tea, sit around a simple tea table, sip at will, and talk casually, dispelling the fatigue of a day's work. Although the methods of drinking tea are different, the pleasure caused by tea is the same.

But there are many things to pay attention to when drinking tea, and the most particular ones are probably the people of Fujian. I remember when I was at home, living a quiet life in my study, with bright windows and a clean space, I often used small Yixing teapots as big as oranges, snow-white tea cups as small as lychees, celadon porcelain bowls and plates from the Chenghua and Xuande periods with wrinkled patterns, teapot mats woven from dragon eye rushes or cogon grass, and copper-tin canisters, arranged randomly on the tea tray. I selected famous Wuyi Mountain rock tea varieties, heated them in a red kiln, and took dried cogon grass or charcoal core, stuffed it into the cracks and burned it. I placed a jade silk pot filled with clear spring water on the stove. When the water was about to boil, I first rinsed the empty teapot, put in the tea leaves, poured in boiling water, covered the spout of the teapot, then poured water on the teapot and small cups, and rotated to wash the cups. Then, I poured the tea, with a color like malachite and smoke like light mist. The fragrant and refreshing taste penetrated my heart and spleen. In front of the misty rain window, with two or three close friends, we slowly sipped together, and ate some candied fruits and light tea snacks. It was really a pleasure to cultivate one's emotions, and all the worldly atmosphere and worries were thrown to the four winds. But in the past ten years or so, I have been living in other places. Although I still drink tea every day, due to the busyness of work, there is actually a lack of opportunity to savor it leisurely. I have no choice but to ignore whether it is good or bad and just casually brew it and drink it. Recalling the Qingfu of the past, I can't help but feel a little disappointed.

Last month, I traveled to West Lake and brought back a few catties of wild tea from Wengjia Village. The taste is more refreshing than ordinary Longjing. I often take a small amount of it during my leisure time in the morning and evening, add rock sugar and rose flowers, put it in a white porcelain covered cup or glass cup, fill it with boiling water, and place it on the table. Watching the curled green leaves float and unfold in the water cup like cellophane noodles, it makes people feel a piece of ice, and the sultry heat is completely eliminated. I feel that it is much better than eating those Ice Wafers. Therefore, I wrote "Tea Chat" to tell the world's friends who have the same hobby.

Fictional Novel

Ordinary Things (11) 203

— Dan Guosun

"It's useless for you and me to argue at this time. Anyway, when things come to a head, there will always be a natural solution. Being tough in words is of no use."

Pei Yu had no choice but to end it like this, but she still couldn't help but say these two sentences:

"If Zhiguang's family had not returned to Hangzhou, then he would not have gone to Zhabei."

"If he didn't go to Zhabei, would things at the factory be better?" Bo Tang said.

(III)

Zhiguang and Bo Tang were both civil engineers who graduated from France. However, Zhiguang initially went there by taking advantage of the work-study opportunity. Before entering a specialized school, he spent several years working in factories in France. Later, he encountered an opportunity and gradually had the mental and material ability to enter a polytechnic in Paris to study civil engineering. He happened to be in the same class as Bo Tang, so they became friends. In terms of temperament, Bo Tang was a generous, upright, and beauty-loving son of a wealthy family, while Zhiguang was a serious, precise, and very considerate scholar from the countryside. In terms of practical interest, Bo Tang's specialty in civil engineering was decorative art, while Zhiguang's specialty in civil engineering was structural planning. Of course, these two reasons can help us understand their personalities, but the benefit of their years of learning and sharpening together at school made them become bosom friends. After returning to China, Bo Tang worked as a technical official in the Xin Jing municipal government for a year, while Zhiguang worked in a construction company in Shanghai. Later, Bo Tang felt that the rise and fall of his career was as uncertain as the wind. It just so happened that he was newly married, and his new wife, Ms. Peiyu, did not approve of the living and eating habits in Xin Jing, so Bo Tang resigned from his official position, embraced Peiyu, and returned to his old residence in Shanghai to live a warm life. After more than half a year, Bo Tang reached a state of being too quiet and wanting to move. He saw that the construction industry in Shanghai was developing day by day, so he took out a portion of his ancestral property and organized the Changxing Construction Factory, and invited Zhiguang to join Changxing and entrusted him with the position of chief engineer.

For three or four years, Changxing's business has been one of the best in Shanghai. Of course, one reason is that Bo Tang relies on his family background and therefore has very long arms, and the second is that their technology is indeed outstanding. However, the fundamental point of Changxing's victory, which is unmatched, is Bo Tang's ability to know people and make good use of them, and Zhiguang's effective management. Zhiguang uses a reasonable system for hiring people on the one hand, and uses a cooperative system for treating people on the other hand. Therefore, the efficiency of work can certainly be high, and the relationship between labor and capital can also be good. When the "January 28th" anti-Japanese incident occurred, Changxing naturally stopped working along with the trend of the entire city. After three or five days, the workers in the factory gradually followed the trend of the enthusiastic men in the city, and some went to join the 19th Route Army. They each contributed their skills, received the command of the officers, and helped those soldiers do some emergency defense work. Zhiguang also did his best to give them many conveniences.

In the face of such a great enemy, these good men who came and went empty-handed and had no worries were truly fearless, especially when they encountered a group of people in foreign clothes and under a different national flag invading our territory. They not only forgot what money was, not only forgot what family was, but even their only self was given to that "we" in their mouths to resist that "they" in their mouths!

However, it seemed that this "we" resisting that "they" could not be resolved in a day or two, so these good men who had rushed from the city to the front line to volunteer felt that simply giving themselves to this "we" could not last. Therefore, they further sought help from those who were close to them. Although the scope of their requests for help clearly identified the words "those who are close to them," they did not expect that the reasons for human beings approaching each other were different, so they were even less concerned about the consciousness of those who were being asked for help. For example, the workers of Changxing Construction Factory asking Bo Tang for help is a clear example.

At about six o'clock this morning, Zhiguang got up and went to the factory first, according to the method agreed upon with Bo Tang last night. He rode his two-wheeled bicycle, and drove more than ten minutes from his residence near Caishi Road, passing through the iron barbed wire gate along the south side of the French Concession, which symbolized a story of nervous anxiety, before arriving near Dananmen. The morning market near Dananmen was still as busy as usual. Although there were many military police with pink collar tabs on the street, the police with white collar tabs seemed to imitate the military police's solemn but gentle attitude towards the citizens because of the presence of the military police. Therefore, every time Zhiguang left any iron barbed wire gate at the southern end of the French Concession, he seemed to only see the police checking for traitors, but he did not see them forcibly seizing the pads of rickshaws. Originally, if there was any small dispute unrelated to national borders on any street in Shanghai, as long as someone said, "We are all family," then the dispute would be resolved immediately.

A disastrous fall to 26 yuan

New Low Prices Reappear

The gold market was turbulent yesterday, with extreme volatility. Initially, both British and American silver prices rose, while in the foreign exchange market, the British pound fell and the US dollar surged. At the Five Metals Exchange, forward silver prices rose by 0.064 yuan. American cotton soared by over 80 points, stocks by over 1 yuan, and American wheat by over 0.01 yuan. Despite reports of the United States considering amendments to gold prohibition laws, the gross price retreated to 0.034 yuan, further dropping to 796.7 yuan. Origin of the Firm Gold Jewelry Market 205

| Shortage of Spot Goods |

| Those Who Have It Don't Want to Keep Much |

| Those Who Seek It Cannot Obtain Much |

While the gold standard has plummeted continuously, gold jewelry in silver shops remains firm. The "cooked red" price has reached an additional 250 yuan or more, a stark contrast to the addition of just over ten taels when the gold market was stable in the past. This indicates that spot goods are extremely scarce, a result of the cutoff of supplies from visiting merchants. Furthermore, spot stores are wary of keeping too much stock due to the wide disparity between the futures and "cooked red" prices. Goods are moving swiftly in ports such as Xiamen and Hong Kong, further diminishing the supply. Additionally, Xiamen customers, seeing the difficulty in securing goods in the gold market, are flocking to silver shops for jewelry, further driving up prices. The current price of gold jewelry, considering the "cooked red" price, the gold standard price, and the silversmith's fee, does not seem excessively high.

Silk and Tea: Vast Discrepancies in Summer Cocoon Production in Jiangsu, Zhejiang

Jiangning Cocoon Production Reaches Its Limit 220

This year's spring cocoon harvest in Jiangning was insufficient. Most silkworm farmers raised summer cocoons as a supplement, but the silkworms were of poor quality, resulting in a remarkably meager cocoon yield. The cocoons were also of lower grade, and cocoon merchants did not collect them. Instead, they were sold to local silk merchants at a cocoon price of only around 20 yuan.

Lake Region Production Uniformly Nine-Tenths of Previous Years 221

This year's summer silkworm rearing in various silkworm areas of the Lake Region was quite prosperous, and cocoon production was abundant. It is uniformly estimated to be nine-tenths of the usual year. The highest cocoon price was 45 or 46 yuan, and the lowest was 28 or 29 yuan. The cocoon market has already concluded.

Foreign Firms' Silk Sales Increasingly Sluggish 222

As foreign exchange rates increase, overseas silk prices continue to decline slightly. Although European firms in Shanghai are importing, Chinese silk merchants are holding back from selling due to the low prices. The market atmosphere is sluggish and quiet. French firms are on holiday. Yesterday, only English firms and others imported 20 bales of Shanghai white factory silk and 20 bales of Sichuan yellow factory silk. The prices remain relatively stable.

Slight Fluctuations in the Tea Market 223

The Student Uprising at Tokyo Imperial University Intensifies 243

▲Hatoyama Decides to Request Massive Arrests of Students by Japanese Police

(Hualian News Agency, Tokyo, 13th) The student uprising at Kyoto Imperial University has intensified due to Education Minister Hatoyama's barbaric measures in dismissing six professors, triggering public outrage. Hatoyama yesterday ordered provincial education officials to go to Kyoto and met with President Matsui for five hours today. He also discussed with the head of the student affairs section, Abe, and decided to take high-pressure measures by requesting the police to conduct massive arrests of students to suppress the student uprising. However, graduates are still helping students and professors, so the future is still difficult to resolve.

National Translation and Compilation Bureau Relocates Entirely 245

After the Ministry of Education's Compilation and Examination Department was reorganized into the National Translation and Compilation Bureau, it was divided into two offices. The General Affairs Office remained within the Ministry of Education, while the Compilation and Examination Office moved to the Overseas Chinese Guesthouse behind the Drum Tower, near the municipal government's designated residential area on Shanxi Road. The area is spacious, sparsely populated, and has fresh air, making it very suitable for the bureau's staff to reside and work there. Director Xin Shuzhi found it inconvenient to have the bureau split into two locations, as he had to travel between them daily, and the various groups at both locations also experienced difficulties in coordinating matters. Therefore, he slightly expanded the existing housing at the Compilation and Examination Office on Shanxi Road, which is currently under renovation. It is reported that the General Affairs Office, currently located in the Ministry of Education, will be moved to Shanxi Road next week to consolidate operations. The Ministry of Education will then use the vacated space to establish a Inspectorate, which will be used for storing archives.

The Board of Directors of the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture will hold its ninth annual meeting in Shanghai at 9:00 AM today (the 14th). The Ministry of Education has sent Shen Pengfei, Director of Higher Education, to attend as a representative.

China Education Association Expresses Condolences to Ma Zhanshan 249

▲And Offers Several Suggestions for Future Resistance Against Japan

▲Ma States that as Long as He has a Breath Left, He Will Never Slacken in Resisting Japan

The Shanghai Chinese Secondary School Faculty and Staff Association specially sent representatives Xu Zexiang, Wu Baojin, Shen Zulei, Liu Zirun, and others to visit General Ma Zhanshan at 11:00 AM yesterday to express condolences and offer several suggestions for future resistance against Japan. Mr. Ma received them, and the association's representatives first stated their purpose and inquired about his views on future resistance efforts. Mr. Ma replied as follows: ㈠ He expressed his deep gratitude for the support of the Shanghai people. ㈡ He hoped that the entire country would unite sincerely and fight to the end in future resistance efforts. ㈢ Japan's ambition is insatiable, and China can only survive through resistance. ㈣ As long as he has a breath left, he will never slacken in the work of resisting Japan. He hopes for the guidance and assistance of his compatriots. Finally, the association's representatives expressed their hope that Mr. Ma would carry out his original intention to kill the enemy, recover lost territory, and not betray the expectations of the people. After a long and cordial conversation, they took their leave. It is reported that the association plans to visit Generals Su Bingwen and Li Du within the next few days.

Jida University Introduces New Preferential Measures for Overseas Chinese Students 250

▲Students from Various Places are Sending Letters Requesting Enrollment Brochures

National Jinan University's recruitment of new students for this year, specifically for overseas Chinese students, will begin on August 2nd, 3rd, 4th, and 5th, and the examinations will be held on the 7th and 8th. Previous reports have covered these details. It is learned that the school, as the highest institution of higher learning for overseas Chinese, has the primary goal of cultivating overseas Chinese students. Due to the prevailing economic downturn in various overseas regions, many overseas Chinese parents feel financially burdened, and there is a lack of clear understanding of the domestic security situation. Fearing that overseas Chinese students may not be very enthusiastic about returning to China for education, the school has introduced new preferential measures to provide relief and encourage overseas Chinese students to return to China: ㈠ Transfer students: In addition to enrolling first-year students in the university, the Faculties of Arts, Sciences, and Commerce will also enroll overseas Chinese transfer students in the second and third years. The middle school department will fully enroll overseas Chinese students. In addition to third-year high school and junior high students, each grade will also enroll overseas Chinese transfer students. ㈡ Tuition exemption: All overseas Chinese students studying in the school's university or middle school departments, whose families are poor and whose circumstances are verified to be true, may be granted reduced or waived tuition fees, depending on the situation. ㈢ Registration and examination dates and locations: The registration for the aforementioned transfer students will be held at the same time as this year's recruitment of overseas Chinese students (August 2nd, 3rd, 4th, and 5th), and the examinations will be held on August 7th and 8th. Those who are unable to arrive in time due to unforeseen circumstances may arrive at the school before August 15th, state the reason, and schedule a supplementary examination. Those who fail the examination may have special remedial measures arranged. The registration and examination locations are both at the school's campus in Zhenru, Shanghai.

Opening Ceremony of the Second Municipal People's School of the Municipal Education Association 251

▲40 Students, Mostly Rickshaw Pullers

▲The School Plans to Experiment with Implementing Education for Rickshaw Pullers

Since promoting the "One-One Education" movement, the Municipal Education Association has been making tireless efforts to implement it. Its Second Municipal People's School, since Principal Chen Rongfa took office, has been borrowing the Puyu Primary School in Sanminfang, Puyu East Road, as its campus. The preparations have been completed, and classes officially began on July 10th. A supplementary opening ceremony was held yesterday (the 12th) at 7:00 PM, attended by over 40 teachers and students, and Municipal Education Association representative Zhang Lichun. After the formalities were completed, Principal Chen reported on the preparation process, the school's situation, and its plans. This was followed by a speech by Municipal Education Association representative Zhang Lichun, titled "The Significance of the Municipal Education Association's 'One-One Education' Movement and the Awareness that Students of People's Schools Should Have." It is also reported that 35 of the 40 students at the school are rickshaw pullers, and the school is an experiment in education for rickshaw pullers. It is noted that the establishment of education for rickshaw pullers in Shanghai is an unprecedented pioneering endeavor by the school.

A Further Statement from the Chengzhong School Board of Trustees 252

A letter from the private Chengzhong Middle School Board of Trustees reads: We respectfully begin by stating that we have read the article "Former Chengzhong Principal Ge States the Process of Hiring Faculty and Staff" in your esteemed newspaper on July 8th. Our board feels compelled to clarify certain factual inaccuracies. According to our school's established practice, all faculty and staff appointment letters should be jointly signed by the principal and the head of academic affairs. After former Principal Li took office in August of the 20th year, he reviewed the contracts of all faculty and staff and discovered that they had all been issued separately by former Principal Ge. The letters were dated August 1st. However, former Principal Ge had already resigned before August 1st, and the head of academic affairs had also left the school in July. Former Principal Li considered that these appointment procedures were not in compliance. Following the usual practice when new and old principals transition at the beginning of a school term, he deemed them invalid. Therefore, he re-hired more than sixty faculty and staff members. Only about ten were not re-hired. Who knew that these un-rehired faculty and staff members would insist that the appointment letters sent in advance by former Principal Ge should be valid? Thus, the dispute arose. This is how the case initially unfolded. From the beginning of the incident, our board clearly stated that it was difficult to immediately determine which procedures were legal: those of the current Principal Li or those of the departing Principal Ge. However, we sincerely hoped that all parties would set aside legal arguments and focus on reconciliation to resolve the matter. Now, the Supreme Court has ruled that the un-rehired faculty and staff members had been certified by former Principal Ge and that the appointment letters, though dated August 1st, were actually sent in late June, and therefore valid. Our school will, of course, abide by the judgment and assume responsibility for the un-rehired faculty and staff members. However, whether the school's loss was due to the negligence of former Principal Li or the error in the procedures of former Principal Ge's sending the appointment letters is another legal question for which society will render its fair judgment. As for former Principal Ge's statements, they contain many discrepancies with the facts. 1) Former Principal Ge claimed to have resigned on July 10th of the 20th year and issued appointment letters in late June of the same year. However, our board confirms that it received the resignation letter, signed by former Principal Ge and written by school staff, on June 26th of that year, not July 10th. The sending of appointment letters also occurred at that time. 2) Our board always consults with the principal to jointly decide on increases or decreases in important school positions, as they affect the budget. However, we never interfere with personnel matters. 3) Although our board sincerely and repeatedly urged former Principal Ge to stay when he resigned, after he left office, our colleagues, remembering his four years as principal and believing he deeply loved the school, gifted him a generous sum and allowed him to rent a school-owned house near the school, hoping he could continue to care for the school at any time. Unfortunately, since the school dispute arose, we have only heard of former Principal Ge repeatedly contacting the Education Bureau and the un-rehired faculty and staff members. He has not once consulted with our board, which our colleagues cannot help but regret. However, we dare not criticize former Principal Ge's "character" in the slightest. In short, for the past two years, the turmoil during former Principal Li's tenure had already left us exhausted. After the January 28th Incident, we have still been unable to collect rent on school property. Our colleagues are truly overwhelmed. We hope that members of society will consider the difficulties faced by the school's founder in establishing the school and offer assistance when possible. Our colleagues will, of course, uphold our original intention of protecting the school and work even harder. We are unwilling to engage in any further pointless arguments in writing. Sincerely, to the editor of the Shenbao Education News Column, from the private Chengzhong Middle School Board of Trustees, July 12th.

Letter from Jiangsu Provincial Shanghai Middle School 253

A letter from Jiangsu Provincial Shanghai Middle School reads: We respectfully begin by stating that we have read the news article "Jiangsu Provincial Middle School Principal Seeks a Way Out for Students Who Failed One Subject in the Joint Entrance Examination" in your newspaper's Education News column on July 12th. It states that our school ranked first in the overall average score of the Jiangsu Provincial Joint Entrance Examination for graduates. However, the Education Department has not yet completed the statistics for the Jiangsu Provincial Joint Entrance Examination results, nor has it published them. Therefore, the mentioned claim appears to be inconsistent with the facts. We hereby issue a statement to request a correction to be published in the Education News column. Sincerely, to the editor of the Shenbao Education News Column, from Jiangsu Provincial Shanghai Middle School, July 13th.

Spring and Autumn

A Fine Tale of the Zhuli Plum 257

— Zhan Lu

There is Still the Fragrance of Xi Shi's Fingernails

Summer is truly the world of fruits. The signs on the fruit stalls are like the marquees outside theaters, advertising famous actors. The Zhuli plum is a seasonal delicacy, so the four characters "Jiaxing Zhuli Plum" on the fruit stalls are written with especially vigorous brushstrokes, easily catching the eyes of passersby.

"There is still the fragrance of Xi Shi's fingernails," is a famous line from an ancient poem praising the Zhuli plum of the Jingxiang Temple. Although the Zhuli plum is native to Jiaxing, the ones produced by Jingxiang Temple are considered the best. Jingxiang Temple's Zhuli plums have a special mark: the imprints of Xi Shi's pinch, with varying thickness and length, much like the marks of Emperor Xuanzong's fingernails on the back of the Kaiyuan Tongbao coins of the Tang Dynasty. Chinese people worship beauties, and there are always many legends. Some say it's Xi Shi's fingernail marks, and everyone believes it to be true. Especially scholars and literati regard it as a unique and excellent subject. Moreover, Mr. Zhu Zhuchu's "Songs of the Yuanhu Boat" says: "It is said that Xi Shi once pinched them, and to this day, every plum has fingernail marks." Hanging Xi Shi's name further enhances the value of Jingxiang Temple's Zhuli plums.

Since the best variety of Zhuli plum is in the Buddhist temple, officials constantly demanded them, with hardly a peaceful year. There were officials who would pre-seal the courtyards where the plums were produced with red stamps, thinking that this would ensure that all the fruits belonged to the government. But when the Zhuli plums ripened and they unsealed the yards to pick the fruits, there wasn't a single one left on the branches. This was because, since the Zhuli plum was so precious, it had to be irrigated daily after it bore fruit, and measures had to be taken to drive away flocks of birds, otherwise they would eat all the plums. The ignorant officials didn't understand why, and thought the monks had secretly picked the plums. They immediately forced the monks to kneel down and beat their bald buttocks. The monks, feeling wronged, wanted to cut down all the trees to eliminate the source of trouble. Mr. Zhu Zhuchu's preface to "Ode to the Zhuli Plum" states: "Recently, suffering from the demands of officials, the monks have cut down many of the trees, and I worry that there will be none left in the future." This explains the situation.

There is also a ridiculous anecdote about the Zhuli plum: During the Qing Dynasty, Zhejiang suffered from continuous rain, similar to the current "water, water everywhere" era. A governor said to his subordinate: "This year, the disaster victims are suffering greatly." The Magistrate of Jiaxing stepped forward and said: "Reporting to Your Excellency, the disaster victims in my county are not suffering." The governor laughed and said: "Since they are called disaster victims, how can they not be suffering?" After returning to his office, the magistrate found two baskets of the best Jingxiang Temple Zhuli plums and presented them to the governor, saying: "Please try these, Your Excellency. The Zhuli plums in my county are truly not bitter." The governor laughed, knowing that he had mistaken "disaster victims" for "Zhuli plums that are not bitter". Before long, he impeached the magistrate for neglecting his duties. The magistrate who had misunderstood "disaster victims" became a "disaster official" himself.

Ghost Stories 258

— Yongzi

Speaking of ghost stories, naturally our China is the most developed in this area. The new ghosts are big, the old ghosts are small, and since China's Pangu to the Three Sovereigns and Five Emperors, up until the 22nd year of the Republic of China, there are so many years, months, days, and hours that who knows how many myriads upon myriads of ghosts both big and small there have been in the end? Unless one inquires of the Yanluo Wang who sits high and solemnly in the Hall of Souls, nobody would be able to know.

China's ghost stories – should several doctors, masters, and bachelors come together to compile a book, even the grand compilation of the Siku Quanshu would be hard-pressed to take sole pride of place. For instance, the ghostly underworld that has been passed down among the common people would cause even those foreign academy editors who compiled the Encyclopedia Britannica to feel shame for their lack of education. In the vast and boundless underworld, there is the Meng Po Pavilion, the Village of Evil Dogs, the Bridge of Helplessness, the Pool of Blood River, the Mountain of Sharp Blades, the Bewildering Array, the Platform of Longing for Home, the Fiery Inferno, the Eighteen Levels of Hell, the Six Paths of Reincarnation, and other great places. Although Arctic exploration teams, Himalayan exploration teams, and even Christopher Columbus, the Big Brother who discovered the New World, have not had the honor of visiting, our Emperor Taizong of the Great Tang once toured this place. If you, gentlemen, do not believe me, let The Journey to the West serve as proof.

As for the types of ghosts, like the complex circumstances of the ethnic groups of the world, there is also a wide variety. Big-headed ghosts, small-headed ghosts, hanged ghosts, wall-touching ghosts, starving ghosts, drowning ghosts, fire-burned ghosts, consumption-disease ghosts, and all sorts of forms and appearances – everything that one could want is available. In addition, there are battlefield ghosts that often wail, and aristocratic ghosts in great Chang'an mansions that can be heard when the sky is overcast. These ghosts are so many that they simply cannot be listed one by one. If you, readers, do not believe me, please see the Ullambana Festival during the Ghost Festival.

These things, those things, all have reliable evidence. If you say that it is superstition, that is truly a sin, and after death you will have to enter the hell of tongue-plucking, the Avici Hell. Please see, in the Chilean parliament, just last month two thousand fire-burned ghosts disturbed the parliamentarians to the extent that their hair stood on end and not a single one of them could stay at their seats peacefully. One can know that when a person dies, he becomes a ghost – this is an unbreakable truth.

Originally, this world is already full of gambling ghosts, lustful ghosts, opium-smoking ghosts, poverty ghosts, greedy ghosts, and snobbish ghosts. Between the human world that is hell and the ghostly underworld, humans are already few and ghosts are many, and for the ghostly underworld, it goes without saying.

Beneath the blue sky, in the bright and clear world, if one doesn't speak of human things and instead speaks of ghost stories, that, too, has a different flavor.

Surviving Poems from the Jielou 259

— Gengbai

▲Short Nap

A short nap can bring a bit of coolness, reclining in a rattan chair in the center of the room. A patch of green at the door suggests tranquility, while the scorching sun outside is wildly intense. To be still is to forget desire, and to live in peace is to know what you will lose. One lifetime of seeing things is to truly believe that, to pull wind and thunder to make a scene.

▲An Impression from Looking out over the Sassoon Building

Lights on a thousand streets the night is yet not over, alone I lean on the railing above the thirteen stories. The windows where the people reside look like honeycombs, looking down upon them the structure looms as a bird’s path. Nearly exhausted is our nation it is fitting it comes to this, in the end dirtying the soil how could it not have a start? The land where a thousand men spill sweat and blood, who will allow him to get one peaceful breath?

Croaking Frogs 260

— Zhen

Zhao Shixiu has two lines of poetry that say, "During the yellow plum season, rain falls in every home, green grass ponds are filled with frogs." These lines have been popular for a long time. Right now, it is the "rain in every home" season, and naturally the entire world is also filled with "frogs everywhere."

Originally, frogs are amphibians. Throughout the year, you can see their tracks at any time or place, so there’s nothing special about that. But during this plum rain season, it is their most fertile, most expansive season. Here "Gok! Gok! Gok!" There "Gok! Gok! Gok!" Everywhere one can hear a continuous chorus of frogs. Who can say the present time is not a "world of croaking frogs?"

Su Dongpo said: "The swallows begin to nest on the painted rafters, the abandoned swamp is already filled with croaking frogs." Jia Dao said: "Meeting egrets after the rain, hearing the distant croaking frogs in the deep night." These are both understated statements about croaking frogs, neither affirming nor denying, not uttering a word of praise.

To compare a group of croaking frogs to people, old poems that contain deep meanings should take the few lines left by Lu You as the starting point for breaking through previous people's records. Lu You said: "Affectionate grass grows green along the wall; brazen frogs croak around the house." Again, he said, "The mind is like an old horse, though it knows the way; the body is like a croaking frog, not belonging to the officials." There are words within words here; there are sounds beyond the strings, which should be carefully savored! One praises, one criticizes, the statements appearing to contradict each other before and after! In fact, guessing the poet's main point, I fear that the compassionate feeling toward the croaking frogs holds more weight. Because so-called "brazen" can only be interpreted as "bored," and is different from the meaning when we now scold someone for being "brazen." Saying that the croaking frogs around the hut let out bored groans, of course, can be considered a completely critical tone. As for the latter statements that "the body is like a croaking frog, not belonging to the officials," that is not only feeling sympathy for the frogs, but also directly comparing one's self to a croaking frog.

People who live in ivory towers or golden houses are unlikely to have much affection for croaking frogs; however, regardless of whether you feel affection or not, as long as the plum rain season comes, they come out to shout, forming a continuous chorus, not willing to be dull, and noisily cheering. Since ancient times, this has long been an "ironclad fact."

Small Inn 261

— Huang Kewei

A milky white lightbulb is covered in a layer of dust, weakly emitting a dim ray of light.

On the door, a faded red piece of paper is pasted, on which is written:

"Exclusively serving traveling merchants." "Accommodation fee: one dime per night." There are no attendants, no elevators. Stepping inside, one can see the double-layered wooden beds connected together. On the stiff poplar planks is spread a mat (in the summer). A broken quilt, like a dead snake, is rolled up on one side. The walls are covered with bedbug blood, mixed with a few yellow spots scorched by cigarette butts. In several places, sentences expressing complaints are written.

···Misfortune upon misfortune···Desperate straits···Empty pockets···

···What to do, what to do···Don't laugh at my poverty···Don't look down on me···Eat my old fist···Snobbish dogs···

On the floor, thick phlegm is spat everywhere, sticking to several half-dead bedbugs. Coughing sounds are heard like a string of firecrackers, and sighs and snores mix together.

In this place, there is no peaceful life, only pain and annoyance, like poisonous snakes, gnawing at someone's soul.

The small inn is the dormitory for poor friends who have been squeezed out of big hotels, and it is the headquarters for blood-sucking bedbugs.

▲Correction: In yesterday's publication, "Philippine and Ham," ham was mistaken for [a character meaning foul or fishy]. This must be corrected immediately.

Wheresoe'er I Roam

Travelogue of the World's Fair (III) 262

— Huang Juemin

(6) In addition, an airfield was specially built for visitors to take aerial tours. The fee was three yuan for every twenty miles. I had always regretted never having flown in an airplane, so I decided to try it. I felt that the speed of 120 miles per hour was very fast to watch, but seemed very slow when sitting in it. On June 13th, a wireless telegram was received on the President Hoover ship, stating that one of the planes had crashed on the 12th. All eight passengers, five men and three women, as well as the pilot and co-pilot, were burned to death. If I had accepted a friend's invitation to return to China on the President Hoover on June 16th, then the 12th would have been the planned day to tour the World's Fair, and I might have also been in danger. Now that I have been spared from disaster, it is indeed fortunate.

(7) Long-distance telephones were also available inside the Transportation Exhibition Hall. You could call any of the forty-eight major cities in the United States for free. Driven by curiosity, I waited for two hours to get my turn to try making a long-distance call from Chicago to Mr. Chen Jiyi, a classmate at 430 West 24th Street in New York City. Unexpectedly, Mr. Chen was out at the time and I couldn't reach him. Fortunately, the operator allowed me to try another call. I successfully spoke to Mr. Jin Shurong at the Livingstone dormitory of Columbia University for three minutes. I could hear everything Mr. Jin said very clearly, just like making a phone call in New York. However, Mr. Jin could only hear me vaguely, so in the three minutes, I could only ask Mr. Jin to relay to my friends at the Chinese Education Society of Teachers College, Columbia University, that I was using a free long-distance phone at the Chicago World's Fair to send them my regards.

(4) Social Science Exhibition Hall

Here, visitors can see the life of humans living in caves and the wilderness 5,000 years ago, and the initial family conditions of Americans. From oil lamps to electric lights, radios, automobiles, refrigerators, and household appliances, everything is displayed to show the progress of family life. Other social issues, such as the accumulation and distribution of capital, the process of immigration, the development of education, the latest types of housing and how they will be improved in the future, as well as model villages, are presented clearly using charts or models.

The exhibits here focus on the family life of Americans. Upon entering the first floor, visitors immediately see the family life of Americans during the colonial era. Spinning, sewing, gathering firewood, and cooking were all done by hand. Further in, on one side, is a display of American rural life, such as churches, schools, horse-drawn carriages, and neighborhoods. On the other side, you can see a huge building in the city in 1933 that can house dozens or hundreds of families. Urban life is also very different from rural life. Factories, schools, parks, playgrounds, entertainment venues, flower paths, automobiles, trains, radios, airplanes, etc., are all available for people to enjoy.

Further in, you see a section of an ancient cave from 50,000 years ago, brought from Europe and displayed. It is slightly similar to the caves built by Native Americans in central Illinois.

Next, you see an animated film. It shows the rapid increase in the population of immigrants coming to America, and the resulting problems of transportation, housing, schools, crime, race, and health, as well as how the government solves them, so that people know that the money they pay in taxes to support the government actually yields many times more in return.

Outside the hall, but still belonging to the social science section, is a model of the thousand-year-old Mayan temple, a village of American Indians, and the Lama Temple of Jehol in China. (Picture 2)

The Four Leaders of the Northeast 263

Chapter 11: Bowing in Agreement to Marriage, Deep Concern for the Soldiers, a Joyous Atmosphere

Tian Qing laughed: "You must be missing your wife terribly, right? Why are you so angry?" Zhao Ziqiang shook his head and said: "I'm not joking. If I had any other way, I wouldn't be holding a gun. I heard that the Commander-in-Chief is coming for inspection, so all the battalions are desperately replenishing their ranks. My company has replenished twenty brothers, but damn it, none of them are worth a damn. Not to mention anything else, after teaching them for two weeks, they still can't even handle the household registration book." (Note: A soldier's three-generation resume is called a "household registration book" in military slang, also called a "roster.") Tian Qing laughed: "My company is slightly better, but there are still one or two useless guys. Don't be impatient, just teach them slowly." Zhao Ziqiang said: "I have no patience left. I listened to you and didn't hit them, because hitting them will make them lose face, but..." As he was saying this, two new recruits happened to pass by the window, raising their hands in salute. Zhao Ziqiang said: "Come in, I want to ask you something." The two soldiers walked to the door and stood at attention. The one in front was tall, with a dark face, but with a pair of pale eyes. Zhao Ziqiang said: "You are the worst. Don't panic, slowly recite your household registration book. Just treat it as a normal conversation, don't lie. What is your surname and what is your name?" He said: "My name is Da Ge'er Li (Big Guy Li)." Tian Qing, standing behind, couldn't help but burst out laughing. Zhao Ziqiang turned his head and frowned at Tian Qing, saying: "Listen to him, what will I do if the Commander-in-Chief checks him during the inspection?" That Da Ge'er, straightened his body, rolled his eyes, and couldn't say a word. Zhao Ziqiang coughed and said: "When you were pulling rickshaws outside, you were called Da Ge'er Li, but are you still called Da Ge'er Li now that you're a soldier? Have the platoon leader and squad leader been talking to a log for the past two weeks?" Da Ge'er Li said: "Platoon... what do you call him?" He said: "My name is Li Changfa." Tian Qing couldn't help but interrupt: "Don't add that 'la' character." Zhao Ziqiang nodded and said: "Just make do with it. Who is your guarantor?" He said: "My guarantor is Zhang Sande." Zhao Ziqiang said: "Where are you from?" "I'm from Jinan Prefecture, Shandong." "How old are you?" "Twenty-nine years old." "Who is your grandfather?" (129)

On Entertainment 264

— Wu

A few days ago, I accidentally heard a poor friend say that he wanted to sell a manuscript to buy a phonograph. At the time, I was a little surprised. I thought, to sell one's own hard work to buy an unimportant entertainment item, isn't that crazy? Is listening to Dr. X's "Farewell My Concubine" or "Su San Starts Her Journey" more important than eating? My poor friend is like this, so those brothers who don't have to sell manuscripts and still have food to eat certainly won't ignore the true meaning of entertainment in life.

Indeed, in recent years, entertainment has been given a much higher status. It is said that entertainment is not only enough to make people laugh and feel happy, but it can also save the country. From this, we can see that entertainment is indeed comparable to "chanting scriptures" and other things. However, China's chronic illness is too deep. Although there is such a wonderful way to save the country, it still inevitably allows loyal comrades of the rebellious party to establish a "puppet state," and it is said that the "East China Republic" is also in the works. From this point of view, it has failed the lonely and painstaking efforts of those who advocate entertainment to save the country, which is truly lamentable.

However, those who believe that entertainment has the miraculous effect of saving the country are smart people who deeply understand the truth of entertainment. They have studied this path extremely thoroughly throughout their lives. Take dancing, for example. They know which dance hall is the most luxurious. They fully understand where it is suitable to open a dance hall for a country-saving entertainment show, and where it is suitable to hold a coronation ceremony for a movie queen. As for which is Mei Lanfang's signature play, which star is the Hollywood queen of 1933, and who is this year's president of the flower country (probably changed to chairman in order to adapt to the times), they naturally know them all like the back of their hand, knowing everything and understanding everything.

It is very clear that entertainment is limited to playboys or masters, mistresses, and young ladies, because only these outstanding people have the full possibility of entertainment. They have money and time, and they have energy and interest. They cannot be excited without entertainment, and they cannot live without entertainment. They deeply understand the essence of this, and they feel that in the Three Principles of the People of saving the country and saving the people, it is necessary to add a clause of entertainment. In short, current enter

tainment is completely popular for this group of high-class Chinese. Just looking at the suits worth hundreds of yuan and the cheongsams of 1933 style crowded in front of the Great Light Gate can prove the urgency of this group for entertainment. As for friends who work hard all day and can't afford two dimes to watch Luo Ke drive fast, they can only wear straw sandals and wave palm-leaf fans, standing in groups in front of foreign goods stores listening to the ten-teaching songs of the "hee hee" and "ha ha" radio broadcasts. Besides this, what other opportunities do they have for entertainment?

It seems that more articles can be written on this topic, but I have to stop here today.

The Entrance to the Swimming Pool 265

— Xiangyun

"Old Zhang! Forget it, let's come again tomorrow!" A-Yun was so crowded that he couldn't even breathe, and the front was still piled with dense crowds of people; he despaired and said to his companion who was squeezed in front of him, gasping for air. Beads of sweat dripped from his greasy forehead.

This was the entrance to the swimming pool on the edge of the road going to Jiangwan. The sun was in the blue sky, releasing the heat of 97.7 degrees on the thermometer.

"There's no way, even if we want to go back now, we can't. It's better to squeeze forward hard!" Old Zhang turned his head and said, and then continued his work.

"Good heavens, it's half a dollar for one person, and there are so many people!" A-Yun looked at the situation and knew that it was not easy to go back. So he began to mutter, "The beggars on the road, hearing 'Old Master' this and 'Madam' that, don't even want to give them a penny!..."

The turnstile was constantly calling. Men and women were struggling to be rolled in one by one. The sound of buying tickets, the sound of shouting, the sound of snoring... combined, they just spread into the room.

"Old Zhang! You go buy the tickets first!" Old Zheng, a small man who was pressed so hard behind A-Yun that even his shadow couldn't be seen, said, straining to grab A-Yun's shoulders and standing on tiptoe.

After hearing this, Old Zhang squeezed forward even harder. Like charging into battle.

"Hey! Buy one ticket!"

"Hey! Ticket, one dollar!"

Old Zhang had gradually squeezed closer. Raising his hand and stretching it forward, there was a dollar in his palm. He began to shout.

A-Yun and Old Zheng followed behind the people and crowded up. The number of people in front of them gradually decreased. Finally, they received the tickets handed over by Old Zhang and were rolled in.

"Ah! There are so many people on Sundays!" Old Zhang smiled and said to them when he saw that they had all entered.

"Good heavens, even bank runs don't look like this!" A-Yun said, wiping his sweat and humming with anger.

"Never mind it, let's quickly go change our clothes!" Old Zheng said resentfully.

Lovers in front of the Grand Theatre, the aroma of incense, the Grand Theatre cinema

Lifting their feet and taking steps, they ran towards the changing room, with bright eyes showing happy smiles.

The Suffering of the People 266

— Cheng Luding

After the January 28th Incident, I left Shanghai and returned to Sichuan, staying in the interior for about half a year. There is nothing worth mentioning about my uneventful life, but I gained a deeper understanding of the suffering of the people in the interior. The following "Song of the Old Farmer" is based on real events, but I am not eloquent enough to express their grief and indignation even by a ten-thousandth. However, it can also be seen how the people of Sichuan suffer. The skill or clumsiness of the poem is not what matters. "The sky is like fire north and south of the Yangtze River, the fields are covered with clouds of sorrow. Ten thousand wells are abandoned to seek new springs, the old farmer sadly weeps before me. I am heartbroken and secretly shed tears, bearing the sorrow and feigning joy to face the old man. The old man said, 'Let us sit in this forest and talk about the past and present. I remember when I was young, the customs were pure and beautiful, and life was happy. It would rain every five days and be sunny for ten days, and the four regions were prosperous and had surplus money. In recent years, the weather has changed, and the warlords' sins fill the mountains and seas. Taxes have been collected for fifty years, and the Republic has been around for twenty years. Merchants' business is slow, and fundraising amounts to more than ten million. There is a reason for the tax names, one just finished, another starts again. Repeated wars harm the good crops, making it difficult to sow in the spring and difficult to harvest in the autumn. Farmers dare not use their plows, and the fields are mostly barren. The lives of workers are even more miserable, and they are also "drafted" into military service. Husbands leave their wives and fathers leave their sons, and every family inevitably cries. On weekdays, warlords suppress all sides, confiscating school funds as they please, robbing students and raping women, openly and blatantly. This year's civil war in Chongqing and Luzhou, shooting recklessly regardless of consequences? They also extort ship taxes and donations, destroy cities and burn houses. The warlords are truly heartless, truly powerful and unjust, truly killing people like eating, truly treating civil war like a game. Pitiful people suffer, not distinguishing west from east in the middle of the night. The wandering souls are hazy and the sky is dark, and the wronged blood stains Sichuan red. Even more pitiful is my son, who is always sick, but is called away by the landlord to deliver a message. He only gets a few hundred coins in wages, but loses his life for no reason. Now the land is very dry, there has been no rain for three months and the ditches are empty. After the winter grain is finished, everyone complains, running around to make a living. Suddenly, the sky opens and the sun is at its noon, crawling to the mansion of the rich and powerful, bowing and begging outside the gate, thousands of cries of bitterness and ten thousand cries of bitterness. Who would have thought that the rich and powerful are too vicious, giving no rice and no tea, preferring to feed the yellow dogs with leftovers rather than saving our lives. My seven-year-old grandson's life hangs by a thread, his clothes are torn and his hair is stained with mud, his feet are bare and cold and he cannot walk, calling to the heavens but no one answers, and his mother does not know. Last night, lightning broke the distant mountains, and the electric light flickered and opened the face of the sky. We were happily arranging to weed, but then hail fell and filled the fields. Disasters are coming in droves at the beginning of summer, only adding to the price of rice for the rich and powerful, making a bucket of rice worth ten thousand coins already unbearable, let alone their extravagant desire to be cunning. The seedlings are all lost and green, and the living family is re-planning to drift away, but they are worried about not paying the rent and taxes, and will inevitably sit in the yamen in the future. Sir! Sir, now you know how hard it is to farm, it is better to have money and be happy. It is most difficult to have a bumper year in farming, but with money you can buy high rank. The other day I met a high official in the city, surrounded by guards in beautiful clothes, possessing millions of wealth in an instant, and eating white rice for all "three meals". The brocade curtains shone brightly in the sky, with four or five concubines serving him, all enjoyed because of money, how can it be compared to our suffering?' When I heard the old man's words, my heart was

Page 20

pounded, I tried to persuade the old man to stop his worries. There is nothing to be done in this evil society, but we must strive to eliminate the demons. Descend the demons, with a bang, jump out of this dirty village, save the people, otherwise in the future, our China, the rich and the powerful will oppress even more, please see their satin robes, dyed with the blood of the weak and small. My words, the old man remembers, if the old man does not hear, there was Turkey a few years ago, suffering internal devastation and external oppression, after a national revolution, the people are happy like this, and do you not hear, China now has a revolutionary army, resisting Japan and saving the country to protect the people, although the goal has not yet been achieved, you will soon see the light, the old man's heart began to widen when he heard these words, Yang Chang left and the road was vast,

Modern Celebrity Paintings and Calligraphy XI (in order of receipt) 267

Mr. Wu Zhongxiong's Painting (Brief Biography)

Wu Zhongxiong, from Wuxing, Zhejiang, is the son of the great merchant Wu Shaoqing and the nephew of the famous painter Ren Bonian. He was gifted from birth and could paint as a child. As he grew up, he extensively studied the famous works in his family's collection, and thus became a master in his own right. However, he was unwilling to put his brush down lightly, so those who obtained even a small piece of his work would treasure it as if it were a priceless treasure.

Shop Assistant Correspondence

Striving 268

Mr. Editor;

I previously sent a letter to you asking for your esteemed guidance on the question of "What is the purpose of living in this world?" Yesterday, I read the Shop Assistant Correspondence column in the Shen Bao supplement and saw that the original letter and the answer were published together, which made me very happy! The reply was concise and to the point, and only someone who deeply understands the underlying problems of the current society could achieve this. The layered explanation of the meaning of the word "life" was particularly insightful and unique. However, this question was previously answered by Mr. Ye and Mr. Wei, who said, "The purpose of living in this world, in the final analysis, is to eat." I believe that eating is one of the means to continue survival, not the purpose of life. Now, after the esteemed

Mr.'s answer, "The purpose of living in this world is the word 'life'." Explaining survival with survival seems to be incomplete. It should be known that my asking this question was to pursue the ultimate purpose of life. Because when a person is born, the conditions for life are already in place, and after that, it is only necessary to continue to maintain their survival. Maintaining survival is the right of life, and the essential condition for continuing life. As for the essence of life, it must be elsewhere. I am dull-witted, wandering all night, thinking again and again. Finally, I have a slight clue. I will now reveal it as follows; I sincerely hope for the most guidance, so that the complete answer to this question can be published to the world.

Life is a process of struggle, and the continuous struggle of mankind has created a history of social evolution. If there were no human struggle, then mankind would have been swallowed up by floods and wild beasts long ago, and how could there be today's society? Then today we would still be living in caves and the wilderness, eating raw meat and drinking blood. From the creations of the ancient sage kings to the inventions of modern scientists, all are sufficient to represent the bravest fighters of society. The achievements they have left to us are extremely great! However, although we ordinary people may not have invented amazing technologies in society, we are not completely without contribution or benefit to society: those who are wise and perceptive, create in the front, must rely on those who are perceptive later to execute in the rear. Carrying on the past and starting the future is the responsibility of ordinary people like us, and it cannot be shirked. From the sage kings, virtuous ministers, philosophers, and scholars, to farmers, workers, merchants, and students, peddlers and porters, what they have been engaged in throughout their lives, not neglecting day and night; all are for creating society, promoting civilization, and making a long-term struggle to the death. This kind of fighting spirit, from the reproduction of the nation, is passed down to thousands of generations and no one can replace it. The Book of Changes says: "Strive for self-improvement." Today we say: "Strive hard," although the names are different, they are all the fundamental trends of mankind from birth, not because of different countries, not because of different times. The father passes it on to the son, and the son passes it on to the grandson, thus creating today's solemn and brilliant universe and the record of mankind. Therefore, I say: "Life is a process of struggle"; "What is the purpose of living in this world? To struggle", "Struggle is the fundamental trend of mankind from birth, and therefore there is today's society and today's civilization". A foolish idea, I dare to question

Mr., if I am fortunate enough to be taught further, then I will be even more fortunate. I hereby send this letter and wish you

Teachi Liu Xingchuan respectfully

Editor's Note: Struggle is a means, not an end. Without a purpose, there is no struggle. To see someone kill someone, to beat someone you meet, what meaning is there? There must be a purpose, and then attacking the characters who obstruct me from achieving my purpose, then there will be success and meaning. This world has always been a world of competition, not only human beings, but all other animals and plants are constantly in the process of competition and struggle. But what is the purpose of their struggle? Many people often can't say this question. We only need to examine the results of their struggle, and it is not difficult to understand. "Survival of the fittest", this is the result of struggle. Therefore, we can clearly see that the purpose of struggle, or the purpose of life, can be said to be "survival".

The first condition for survival is eating. Therefore, Liu Jun's letter on July 7th introduced the opinions of Mr. Ye and Mr. Wei, saying "The purpose of living in this world, in the final analysis, is to eat." This sentence can of course be said to be "hitting the nail on the head." However, the two words "eating" are very different; when there is no food to eat, we only seek to have food to eat; when we have food to eat, we can't help but want to eat good food or easy food. So if "eating" is the only purpose of life, then being driven by this kind of "bottomless" desire will create a cruel and terrifying world of you robbing me.

Therefore, we believe that after we have food to eat, after we can survive, we must take "what kind of life is meaningful" as the purpose; we should no longer plunder the necessary materials for others' lives to supply my own enjoyment. What we call "living meaningfully" does not refer to the kind of idealism that many dead people used to say, such as "establishing merit and establishing a career", "making a name for oneself for eternity", "honoring ancestors", and "bestowing wives and sons". What we advocate is mutual aid. People who have no food to eat have the right to ask for help; rich people have the obligation to help others.

Novels

Under the Red and Green Lights (26) 269

— Xi Lin

"Nonsense, Jiangbei person, traitor, don't even think about denying it..." A louder voice drowned out the worker's cries.

A fellow secretly took out a small paper packet and slipped it into the worker's pocket in the hustle and bustle. Only Changfa, standing beside him, saw this action clearly, and he secretly praised his subordinate's agility, good fellow!

"I am...I am a worker...I am fighting against the Japanese!"

"Beat him, beat the traitor!"

"Beat him to death!"

"What a traitor!"

The police finally heard the surge of the crowd and one pointed a gun at the worker's chest.

"Beat him! Grab him!"

The worker, panting, his face covered in blood, tried to explain himself!

"It's a real injustice, I work in the Japanese-owned yarn factory, we don't help the Japanese work, we are on strike. They wrongly accuse me of being..."

Another tall man who looked like a worker pushed his way in...

"It's really an injustice, he's from the XX yarn factory...I know him, we all walked out because we refused to work for the Japanese."

A policeman pushed him aside...

"We'll search him."

Sure enough, they found it, taking a paper package from the worker's body.

That pale face showed no surprise, his eyes widened: how could this thing be in my pocket? Suddenly, he shouted:

"This is outrageous, who put it in my pocket..."

The paper package was opened, revealing: several Japanese coins, a chicken feather, a piece of cloth, and the barely legible characters "Jiangbei Headquarters", heaven knows, there was even a sun-shaped stamp on it!

The tall worker also knew he had been framed and shouted:

"This is an injustice, I can swear to the heavens today, he is indeed a worker from XX...someone is framing him..."

"This one must be a traitor too!" Changfa immediately shouted, and many fellows followed suit:

"This one is a traitor too!"

"Beat this accomplice of the traitor to death!"

"Beat him! Beat him!"

"Beat him! Beat him!"

Fists rained down like hailstones.
